<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

	<div class="pure-g">
		<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage --><div ng-if="::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage" ng-class="vm.details.graphicalAbstract ? 			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract --><div ng-if="::vm.details.abstract" class="ng-scope">
				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">This paper presents a novel eco-friendly batteryless remote control (RC) system based on a multi-RF identification (RFID) scheme. The proposed RC device does not require the use of batteries or other installed power source. Instead, it relies on passive RFID chips that are remotely powered by an RFID reader. The controlled device (e.g., a TV) incorporates an RFID reader to power up and communicate with the RC. The proposed batteryless RC is composed of an antenna, a plurality of <i>N</i> passive RFID chips and <i>N</i> switches, and a multi-port microstrip network that interconnects the various RFID chips, allowing them to share a common antenna. Each key of the RC is associated to an RFID with a unique identifier, which allows the device to be controlled to identify the key pressed by the user. The proposed arrangement ensures that only the chip associated to the pressed key is read by the RFID reader, while the other chips remain inactive. First of all, the system is described including the multi-RFID scheme and the proposed multi-port network. Afterword, a characterization of the contact switches and RFID chips is performed. This is followed by RFID chip impedance matching and switch tuning. A multi-port network is fabricated (in low-cost FR4) and measured in order to access network's behavior depending on some parameters such as the number of ports and distance from the active port to the antenna. Finally, a four-key RC unit is prototyped, and an RFID reader system is integrated in a TV by using an external RFID-to-infrared interface. Four control functionalities are implemented and tested (CH+, CH-, Vol+, and Vol-). Measurements are also conducted to evaluate the system coverage range and line-of-sight capability.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->			
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.scope -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Remote control is one of the most widespread convenience devices ever invented. Remote controls (RCs) are used to wirelessly control a variety of devices, such as TVs, doors, game consoles, and air-conditioning equipment, making our daily life easier. Recently, even laptops are equipped with an RC device. Conventionally, RC systems are based on infrared (IR) technology and the controller unit requires batteries for a power source. However, such IR battery-powered systems present several drawbacks, such as the need for direct line-of-sight, the cost associated to battery maintenance, and the limited lifetime of batteries. Most importantly, chemical batteries release toxic waste in the end of their life cycle. Beyond monetary cost, there is thus an environmental price to pay. Disposable batteries take hundreds of years to decompose, and if not properly treated they can seriously risk the public health and the environment.</p><p>A huge number of chemical batteries are used every year. As an illustrative example, consider the case of Portugal, were there is presently 4 million habitual residences. Assuming that 75% of these residences have a TV, 40% have a cable TV Bbox and 30% have hi-fi equipment, we end up with an average of 5.8 million RC devices. Considering two batteries per remote and a battery replacement each six months, we have a total of 23.2 million batteries being wasted every year. It should be noticed that this figure is very conservative since it only takes into account the traditional entertainment equipments. This figure drastically increases if we consider other equipment, such as air-conditioning equipment, game consoles and battery-powered toys, garage doors, and wireless/batteryless keyboards.</p><p>In this sense, eco-friendly solutions must be found to alleviate or even eliminate the battery problem. An approach to mitigate the battery problem in conventional IR technology is to reduce the power consumption of the electronics. This can be done by using an event driven implementation in which the system is always in a sleep mode and is waken up only when the user presses a key. Such approach can extend the battery lifetime and reduce the waste of chemical disposable batteries. Another solution is the use of rechargeable batteries instead of disposable ones. However, this is not cost effective for low-end home devices.</p><p>The first wireless RC invented by Polley in 1955 used a light beam to control a TV <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. At that time, the RF approach was not even a viable alternative due to basic technology limitations. Due to its cost effectiveness and low implementation complexity, the IR technology became preferred and widespread in the past decades. However, as the RF/microwave industry has grown and the price of components have been considerably lowered, radio has became a viable option. It is likely that radio will soon replace IR technology. Due to the advantages of RF technology, namely, long-range two-way communication and non-line-of-sight capability, the industry has started to provide some RF-based RC solutions for home devices. In 2009, ZigBee Alliance and a consortium of consumer electronics manufactures have announced a new technology/standard, especially tailored for home automation, RF4CE. An overview of RF4CE can be found in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>.</p><p>Nevertheless, also in current radio approaches, the use of disposable batteries is still being a drawback. Energy harvesting approach has been proposed to overcome the battery problem. The main research line has been focused on electrical energy harvesting from mechanical strain energy using the piezoelectric effect <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>. For instance, in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>, a prototype is presented in which the energy for powering up the batteryless device is harvested from mechanical energy generated by the user when pressing a piezoelectric harvesting button. It is claimed a generated energy of approximately 1 mJ at 3 V, enough to power up a digital encoder and a radio transmitter for use in batteryless devices such as light switches. A major drawback is related to the frequent necessity of actuating the piezoelectric harvester.</p><p>Several industrial solutions and a few research works have focused on the mitigation of the battery problem. However, very little research has addressed the complete elimination of batteries. In this work, we propose the elimination of batteries by using the wireless power transmission concept. This is inspired by passive RF identification (RFID) systems in which the mobile devices have no battery to power up their electronics. Instead, the required energy is wirelessly delivered by a fixed RFID reader <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>. We precisely propose and prototype a batteryless RC system based on a multi-RFID scheme. The multi-RFID RC scheme is disclosed and both control and interconnection strategies are proposed. We also propose the ways to integrate the RC receiver in the device to be controlled (DeC) (e.g., a TV). Finally, we present a strategy and system to guarantee compatibility with already installed equipments that use IR.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Proposed System</h2></div><p>The proposed RC is based on a multi-RFID approach in which each RFID chip is associated to an RC key, as in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(b)</a>. Alternatively, a passive sensor-alike configuration, as in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(c)</a>, can be used. In such an approach, a key decoder is used and a single RF front-end is shared by the keys. In order to read the tags' ID and to identify the respective key, the DeC, e.g., a TV, incorporates an RFID reader [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(a)</a> ]. As an alternative, the RFID reader can be externally mounted on the DeC as done in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a> [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9(a)</a> ]. This strategy guarantees compliance with already installed equipment by using an RFID-IR adapter. A switch-controlled resonant circuit is used to activate/deactivate each RFID chip [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(a)</a> ]. In order to interconnect the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 0.964em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.84em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula> passive RFID chips of the RC, a multi-port microstrip network [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(b)</a> ] is proposed to guarantee that: by default, all the chips are inactive; once a key is pressed, the respective chip goes to active mode and is read by the reader to identify the pressed key; and the inactive chips do not interfere with the active one.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. Multi-Port Switched Network</h3><p>First of all, a mechanism is needed to allow the user to activate and deactivate the RFID chips. A resonant switch controlled LC circuit is parallel connected to the matched chip. By default, the switch is closed and consequently the series circuit resonates and short circuits the RFID chip. In this state, the chip is unable to respond to the reader. Once the user presses the key, the switch opens and the series circuit no longer resonates. In this state, the reader is allowed to interrogate the chip.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>(a) DeC incorporating an RFID front-end. (b) Diagram of the proposed multi-RFID RC. (c) Alternative passive aensor RC configuration.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6522276/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

vertical-align: -2.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 4.737em;"></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-11">\eqalignno{Z_{\rm IN} &amp; = \left[\matrix{{Z_{0} + jZ_{1} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})\over Z_{0} ({Z_{1} + jZ_{0} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})})} + {Z_{0} + jZ_{2} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})\over Z_{0} ({Z_{2} + jZ_{0} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})})} \hfill\cr \cdots + {Z_{0} + jZ_{n} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})\over Z_{0} ({Z_{n} + jZ_{0} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})})} \cdots + {Z_{0} + jZ_{N} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})\over Z_{0} ({Z_{N} + jZ_{0} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})})}} \right]^{- 1} = Z_{n} = Z_{0} &amp;\hbox{(2)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{Z_{\rm IN} &amp; = \left[\matrix{{Z_{0} + jZ_{1} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})\over Z_{0} ({Z_{1} + jZ_{0} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})})} + {Z_{0} + jZ_{2} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})\over Z_{0} ({Z_{2} + jZ_{0} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})})} \hfill\cr \cdots + {Z_{0} + jZ_{n} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})\over Z_{0} ({Z_{n} + jZ_{0} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})})} \cdots + {Z_{0} + jZ_{N} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})\over Z_{0} ({Z_{N} + jZ_{0} \tan (90^{\circ} + k180^{\circ})})}} \right]^{- 1} = Z_{n} = Z_{0} &amp;\hbox{(2)}}</span></span></disp-formula>similarities exist between the proposed multi-port network and traditional single-pole <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-473" role="math" style="width: 0.964em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.84em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-474"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-475" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-12">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-throw (SPNT) switches <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2a">[8]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_2a">[9]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2a">[10]</a>: this multi-port network could be considered as such a type of switch, connecting one of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-476" role="math" style="width: 0.964em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.84em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-477"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-478" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-13">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula> RFID chips to a single antenna. However, while SPNT switches are electrically controlled (typically using switch diodes), the proposed multi-port is mechanically controlled by the user through contact switches. Furthermore, in our implementation, the termination load of each port in inactive mode is tuned to the operating frequency by using a resonant circuit [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(b)</a> ]. One of the first works in SPNT can be found in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2a">[8]</a>. Later, stub-filter concepts were introduced in order to improve bandwidth performance <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_2a">[9]</a>. This concept has also been used in the RFID field; however, with a different purpose—alternate an RFID reader signal between several antennas <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2a">[10]</a>.<p></p><p>The proposed network meets the following requirements.
</p><ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p>Only the active port <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-479" role="math" style="width: 3.727em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.366em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.25em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-480"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-481" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-482" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-483"><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-485"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-486"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-487" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">i</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-488" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">=</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-489" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-490" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-14">n (Z_{i = n})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> should be routed to the antenna.</p></li><li><p>All other ports do not interfere with port <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-491" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-492"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-493" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-15">n</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and remain invisible to the antenna port.</p></li><li><p>The insertion loss between the antenna port and the active port <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-16-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-494" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-495"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-496" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-16">n</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is ideally 0 dB; the cross-talking between the antenna port and all inactive ports is ideally null and the cross-talking between the active port and all other is ideally null.</p></li><li><p>By default, all ports are terminated with a short, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-497" role="math" style="width: 4.267em; top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-498"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-499"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.985em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-500" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-501"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-502"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-503" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">i</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-504" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">≠</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-505" style="font-size: 70.7%; top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-509"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-510"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.985em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-631"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-632"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-633" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-634" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">(Z_{n} = Z_{0})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is seen by the antenna and all other are invisible. This is true for any key pressed by the user.</p><p>In order to better understand the dynamic routing mechanism involved in the RC circuit, an illustrative example is presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(c)</a>. In this case, a four-key RC is considered and the user has pressed the key number four, forcing the normally closed switch number 4 to be open. Consequently, the impedance termination of branch 4 becomes equal to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-635" role="math" style="width: 1.264em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.14em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-636"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-637"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-638"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-639"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-640" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-641"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-642"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-643" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-26">{Z}_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (corresponding to the impedance of the matched chip RFID4). On the other hand, all other chips are in parallel with a short circuit, imposed by a resonant circuit at the operating frequency, so that the impedance seen by the deactivated branches is zero. These null impedances are transformed into open circuits by the 90° phase shifts imposed by the quarter-wavelength lines. In this sense, the short-circuited chips are deactivated and do not interfere with the rest of the circuit, as can be seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(c)</a>. The crosses represent infinite impedances that do not have an impact in the parallel impedance association. Consider a different scenario, where, for instance, RFID1 or RFID2 is activated and RFID3 and RFID4 are deactivated (by parallel short circuits). In this case, the infinite impedance (open circuit) appearing at the right crossover node would be transposed to the left crossover node by the central half-wavelength line (180° phase shift). Again the infinite impedance would have no effect on the parallel association of impedances and would not interfere with the rest of the circuit. This is in agreement with <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn2" href="#deqn2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a>.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Simulation and Measurement Results</h2></div><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>Custom calibration standards and DUTs mounted on the SMA fixtures.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6522276/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
In this section, the characterization of the switches and the RFID chips is addressed, followed by the chip matching procedure. The previously described multi-port network is simulated and measured and an RC prototype is also measured.<p></p><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Chip and Switch Measurement and Impedance Matching</h3><p>In this work, a G2XN chip (manufacture ref. SL3S1002FTT) has been used. In order to match the chip impedance, its power-dependent <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-644" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.66em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-645"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-646" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-27">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters should be known. Details of UHF RFID chip measurements can be found in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_3a">[11]</a>. It is also important to characterize the RF behavior of the switches. The switch <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-28-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-647" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.66em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-648"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-649" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-28">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters model is extracted and exported to simulations for further evaluation and design. In order to have accurate measurements both for the RFID chips and switches, a calibration procedure is first conducted. Since we are dealing with a noninsertable device-under-test (DUT) and the reference plane must be exactly at the pins of the DUT, a commercial short, open, and thru (SOL) calibration kit is not suitable. For this reason, we have built a custom SOL calibration kit (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>). In such a kit, SMA connectors are used as the fixture for the DUT and for the calibration standards (mounted on the edge of the connectors). This allows the definition of a precise reference plane since both the calibration standards and the DUT are placed at the same physical location. Moreover, this will guarantee a straightforward characterization and specification of the standards in the vector network analyzer (see <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_3a">[12]</a>). To perform calibration and measurements, the calibration standards and DUT are mounted at the top of the SMA connectors (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>). The short standard is obtained by short circuiting the inner SMA conductor to the outer conductor, the open standard is realized by an open-circuit SMA connector and the load standard is build up with a high quality 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-650" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-651"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-652" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-29">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> termination (manufacture ref. CHF1206CNT) on the top of an SMA connector.</p><p>The chip input impedance is depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>. As can be observed, the nonlinear impedance varies with the input power level. Thus, the matching circuit should consider the desired input power level, precisely the minimum input power level required to activate the chip. This information can be drawn from <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> in which the activation point is characterized by an accentuated fluctuation in the real part of the chip input impedance <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_3a">[13]</a>. The knowledge of the unmatched activation point (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-653" role="math" style="width: 7.571em; Point A corresponds to the default closed position in which the switch has a predominant inductive behavior and point B corresponds to the open position in which the switch behaves predominantly as a capacitor. The port termination is formed by the switch-controlled resonant circuit in parallel with the matched chip. As can be seen, the series switch-controlled resonant circuit resonates at 866.6 MHz imposing a short circuit (point C) when the switch is closed. When the switch is open, the impedance is approximately equal to the matched chip (point D), meaning that the series circuit has no significant impact. A simple L-matching circuit is used to match the chip to 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-843" role="math" style="width: 0.929em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.731em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1000.66em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-844"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-845" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6522276/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Measurements of the switch (a) and of the circuit formed by the switch-controlled resonant circuit (switch plus LC circuit) in parallel with the matched RFID chip. When the switch is closed, the series circuit resonates at 866.6 MHz, imposing an approximate short circuit (point C). When the switch is open the input impedance is approximately equal to the matched chip impedance (point D).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6522276/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Multi-Port Simulations and Measurements</h3><p>As a first step, a four-port network is simulated using the ADS simulator, prototyped and measured in order to validate and evaluate the proposed multi-port scheme. In order to reduce the overall circuit size, a meandering technique is used. However, since meandering can cause inter-coupling between the lines, an electromagnetic simulation is also carried out using the Momentum electromagnetic simulator. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6(a)</a> shows the fabricated four-port network. Return loss of the antenna port (P1), <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-846" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-847"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-848"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-849"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-850"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-851" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-852"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-853"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-854" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">11</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">{S}_{11}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and of one of the key ports (P2), <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-855" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-856"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-857"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-858"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-859"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-860" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-861"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-862"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-863" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">22</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">{S}_{22}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, are measured and compared with simulations. The insertion loss <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-864" role="math" style="width: 2.405em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.165em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.04em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-865"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-866" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-867"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-868"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-869"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-870" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-871"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-872"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-873" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">21</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-874" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">({S}_{21})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> between the antenna port and probed key port is also evaluated. Both the simulation and measurement scenarios consider that only one of the keys is pressed by the user. For this purpose, the active port is terminate with 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-875" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-876"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-877" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> both in simulations and measurements<a ref-type="fn" anchor="fn2" class="footnote-link"><sup>2</sup></a> and the remaining ports are terminated with a short circuit to ground by using a via-to-ground. This represents the ideal case in which the series circuit exhibit infinite impedance when the switch is open and zero impedance when the switch is closed. The obtained results are presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6(b)</a>. Simulated and measured return-loss values agree well and indicate a good performance in the band of interest (return loss<a ref-type="fn" anchor="fn3" class="footnote-link"><sup>3</sup></a> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-878" role="math" style="width: 5.709em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.108em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.99em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-879"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-880" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-881" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-882"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-883"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-884"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-885" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-886"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-887"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-888" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">11</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-889" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-890" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-891" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.183em;">|</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-892"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-893"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-894"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-895" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-896"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-897"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-898" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">22</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-899" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-900" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">(\vert {S}_{11}\vert, \vert {S}_{22}\vert)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> below −17 dB). Transmission coefficient <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-901" role="math" style="width: 3.006em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.706em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.59em 2.646em -999.997em); </p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>(a) Four-port network, the antenna port (P1), and one of the key ports (P2) are probed in order to evaluate the return loss and insertion loss. (b) Simulations (solid line) and measurement (crosses) of the four-port network.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6522276/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>In the second scenario, a multi-port with a larger number of ports is built [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7(a)</a> ]. In this case, the objective is to evaluate the performance of the network with respect to parameters as number of ports and distance between antenna port and active port. This allows to evaluate the performance degradation as the number of keys and the distance from the antenna port increases. In order to do so, the following quantities are measured: return loss of the antenna port <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-914" role="math" style="width: 2.405em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.165em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.04em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-915"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-916" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-917"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-918" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-919"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-920"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-921" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">11</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-922" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">(S_{11})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the active port <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-923" role="math" style="width: 3.306em; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-928" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-929"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-930"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-931" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-932" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-933" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">n (S_{nn})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, insertion loss between the antenna port and the active port <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-934" role="math" style="width: 2.465em; top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-935"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-936" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-937"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-938" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-939"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-940"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-941" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-942" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-943" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">(S_{1n})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, isolation between the active port and an adjacent inactive port <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-944" role="math" style="width: 3.426em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.066em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.07em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-945"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-946" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-947"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.646em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-948" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-949"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-950"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-951" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-952" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-953" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-954" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">+</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-955" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">(S_{n,n + 1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and isolation between the antenna and an inactive port adjacent to the active one <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-956" role="math" style="width: 3.727em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.366em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.25em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-957"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-958" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-959"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.586em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-960" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-961"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-962"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-963" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-964" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-965" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-966" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">+</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-967" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-968" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">(S_{1,n + 1})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. All these measurements are made as a function of the active port number or distance from the antenna <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-969" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.26em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-970"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-971" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-972" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-973" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">(n)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The evaluated circuit is depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7(a)</a>. The upper branches are terminated with short circuits simulating inactive ports, while the lower branches are terminated with switch-controlled resonant circuits, allowing the activation/deactivation of the ports during the measurements. In addition, the lower branches are probed through SMA connectors to facilitate the measurements. When not connected to the VNA, the active port <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-50-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-974" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-975"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-976" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-50">n</script></tex-math></inline-formula> or the antenna port is terminated with a 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-977" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-978"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-979" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> load in order to maintain the matching condition <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1a-1b" href="#deqn1a-1b" class="fulltext-link">(1a)</a>. Results are presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a> and <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>(a) Evaluated multi-port network, fabricated in low cost FR4 substrate in a 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-980" role="math" style="width: 0.929em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.731em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1000.66em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-981"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-982" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-52">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> environment. (b) Measured return loss of the antenna port as a function of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-983" role="math" style="width: 0.797em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.599em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.524em 1000.6em 2.384em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-984"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-985" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.754em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">n</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the active port exhibits a similar behavior. (c) Measured insertion loss between the antenna port and the active port. (d) Measured isolation between the antenna and an inactive port adjacent to the active one, the isolation between the active port and an adjacent inactive port present similar values.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6522276/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table I </b>Multi-Port Performance at 884 MHz Depending on Active Port <span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-986" role="math" style="width: 1.723em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.326em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1001.26em 2.715em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-987"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-988" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-989" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-990" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.413em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.421em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">(n)</script><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> summarizes the measured results of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a> for a single frequency (884 MHz). Although the central frequency appears shifted from the initial target (866.6 MHz), the network presents a considerable bandwidth, maintaining good performance at 866.6 MHz. Good return-loss figures are observed both at the antenna port as well as at the active port. The insertion-loss values are also acceptable. Compared to the previous measurement case (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>), the insertion-loss performance is degraded because of the increase in the number of ports, which increases the circuit losses. In the multi-port circuit, as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-991" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-992"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-993" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">n</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increases, the insertion loss also increases. Therefore, there is a distance away from the antenna beyond which the performance is not satisfactory. Although the return loss seems to improve with the increase in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-994" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-995"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-996" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">n</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, this does not represent an effective improvement in the circuit performance since this effect is only a consequence of the restive/insertion loss increasing. Nevertheless, these values are quite acceptable considering the used substrate (FR4), and better performance can be obtained with an improved RF substrate. In terms of isolation, acceptable performance is also achieved. In traditional communication circuits, such values of isolation might not be excellent because very small signal leakage can degrade the communication chain. However, in a passive RFID scenario where a considerable power level is required to supply the chip, such isolation figures are sufficient to bring the power level below the chip activation threshold.</p><p>The multi-port as well as the antenna are designed in a 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-997" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-998"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-999" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> environment. In order to keep the RC design simple and very low cost, a dipole antenna configuration is selected. The antenna is fabricated in an FR4 substrate, matched to 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1000" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1001"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1002" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and afterwards is integrated with the multi-port RC circuit. The absolute value of the reflection coefficient is depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(a)</a>,
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>(a) Simple dipole antenna fabricated in FR4 substrate and respective return loss at 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1003" role="math" style="width: 0.929em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.731em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1000.66em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1004"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1005" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (b) Three-key RC prototype including antenna. (c) Final four-key RC prototype, four TV control functions are implemented (CH+, CH−, Vol+, and Vol−).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6522276/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
indicating good performance at the band of interest. Alternatively to the dipole, a Yagi-alike printed configuration similar to the one in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_3b">[14]</a> can be used to achieve higher gain while maintaining low size and complexity. Final RC prototypes (including antenna) are depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(b)</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">(c)</a>.<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3c"><h3>C. Reading Range Measurements and Robustness Tests</h3><p>Additional measurements have been conducted in an anechoic chamber in order to evaluate the reading range (<a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a>), the impact of several blocking materials in the range (<a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">Table III</a>) and the dependence on the DeC antenna configurations and RC orientation (<a ref-type="table" anchor="table4" class="fulltext-link">Table IV</a>). Using 5.5-dBi circularly-polarized antennas at the DeC transmitter and receiver, a maximum communication distance of 3.5 m has been achieved for a radiated power of 27 dBm. In <a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">Table III</a>, it can be seen that, compared to nonblocked operation (<a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a>), although the range is degraded for cardboard, plastic, and wood blockers, is still possible to maintain communication. On the other hand, metal and the human body completely block the communication. However, all the tested materials inhibit a traditional IR RC to communicate, which was expected since the blocking materials are opaque to IR light.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table2"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table II </b>Reading Range as a Function of Transmitted Power<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-table-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6550039/6522276/6522276-table-2-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>

top: -3.961em; left: 0.003em;"><span style="font-family: MathJax_Size4;">√</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block;
